<span id="freeTextContainer436393533845850791">Name: Sarah Fretz<br/><br/>Citation: Scott, E. (2009). Love you hate you miss you. New York: HarperTeen.<br/><br/>Genre: Contemporary Realistic Fiction<br/><br/>Award: <br/><br/>Format: E-Book<br/><br/>Selection: Living Dead Girl by Elizabeth Scott<br/><br/>Review: <br/><br/>Amy is an extremely “awkward” teenager. She is not very social, her parents are in their own little world and the only thing she has to look forward to is spending time with her best friend Julia. Julia brings out the best in Amy, making her into the person she isn’t…happy, fun, carefree.<br/><br/>But A</span>
  <span id="freeText436393533845850791" style="display:none">Name: Sarah Fretz<br /><br />Citation: Scott, E. (2009). Love you hate you miss you. New York: HarperTeen.<br /><br />Genre: Contemporary Realistic Fiction<br /><br />Award: <br /><br />Format: E-Book<br /><br />Selection: Living Dead Girl by Elizabeth Scott<br /><br />Review: <br /><br />Amy is an extremely “awkward” teenager. She is not very social, her parents are in their own little world and the only thing she has to look forward to is spending time with her best friend Julia. Julia brings out the best in Amy, making her into the person she isn’t…happy, fun, carefree.<br /><br />But Amy is left all alone now. Embracing the fun and carefree life, she becomes an alcoholic and promiscuity to fit in. Only, those actions lead to the death of Julia at the hands of Amy. <br /><br />After completing rehab after Julia’s death, Amy grapples with her now overbearing parents who never seemed to care before but now try to force her to talk about her feelings and spend more time with them. She deals with the stares at school, especially of Julia’s boyfriend and the high school kids who pretend to have been Julia’s friend and are “devastated” by her death. <br /><br />Most of all Amy feels the guilt over killing her friend, even if not intentional. In this book, the reader travels the journey with Amy as she tries to move past her addictions, her guilt and sadness over the loss of her friend. The reader empathizes with her when she is sad, angry, and confused as to how to go on living without the only person Amy feels ever really understood her. Follow Amy on the journey of (re)self-discovery as she faces the future without her friend and what that friendship meant for her future. <br /><br />Recommended.<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/73640946" />
    <a title="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva"><img alt="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392555495p2/1491042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73640946?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=fast-paced-and-engrossing">fast-paced-and-engrossing</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73640946" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9631961660237823026">My thoughts - Amy is a mess. Since the death of her best friend Julia she can hardly function anymore. Everyday seems like one big chore. Life just ins't the same without her and she's having a very hard time coping. You see, Julia was her rock, her support. She made her feel less of a gangly red haired freak, but without her she's left with a bunch of strangers that she has no connection with whatsoever. She feels completely alone. <br/><br/>LOVE YOU HATE YOU MISS YOU was so damn fantastic. This book is </span>
  <span id="freeText9631961660237823026" style="display:none">My thoughts - Amy is a mess. Since the death of her best friend Julia she can hardly function anymore. Everyday seems like one big chore. Life just ins't the same without her and she's having a very hard time coping. You see, Julia was her rock, her support. She made her feel less of a gangly red haired freak, but without her she's left with a bunch of strangers that she has no connection with whatsoever. She feels completely alone. <br /><br />LOVE YOU HATE YOU MISS YOU was so damn fantastic. This book is packed with guilt, anger, sadness and emotion. She blames herself for her best friends death and the therapy sessions aren't getting through to her either. She isn't interested in anything or anyone, but writing these letters to her dead best friends makes things somewhat a little more bearable; therapeutic in a way. <br /><br />I've read this authors previous work and she is extremely talented. This book is a little more gritty than the others but in a good way. I felt so much for Amy. I could relate to her. Loosing my best friend would destroy me, completely. But there is more to it than that. It's only after her death that perhaps Amy gets to know her best friend a little more in realising that maybe she wasn't as perfect as she once thought. <br /><br />Amy's voice is not only wonderful and authentic but refreshing. She is honest and completely herself. She bears all to us and you grow to love and appreciate her for all that she is going through. <br /><br />I am so in love with this book. I think of it often and plan to re - read it very soon &lt;3</span>

<div id="review_64791393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64791393" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2347498-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243137714p2/2347498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64791393?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/2347498-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2347498-laura?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64791393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9667735887451208639">Slightly reminiscent of Speak in tone, Love You Hate You Miss You is a dark book about grief, loss, and personal responsibility. Not nearly as dark as Living Dead Girl, Scott gives us a very realistic story of struggle and grief. After surviving a car accident that kills her best friend, Amy must confront her demons. She struggles with a wealth of problems (alcoholism, her relationship with her parents, school, connecting with others, to name a few) and through that struggle, confronts her feeli</span>
  <span id="freeText9667735887451208639" style="display:none">Slightly reminiscent of Speak in tone, Love You Hate You Miss You is a dark book about grief, loss, and personal responsibility. Not nearly as dark as Living Dead Girl, Scott gives us a very realistic story of struggle and grief. After surviving a car accident that kills her best friend, Amy must confront her demons. She struggles with a wealth of problems (alcoholism, her relationship with her parents, school, connecting with others, to name a few) and through that struggle, confronts her feelings about her best friend and the responsibility she feels for her death.<br /><br />Obviously, this is not a cheery novel. Filled with anger, grief, and all the ugly, hard to talk about emotions, Love You Hate You Miss You can be hard (and frustrating) to read. Despite this, I think it covers some very relevant topics for teens who may be struggling. Amy’s voice is harsh, bitter, and insecure to the core. The growth Amy experiences in Love You Hate You Miss You is not easy for her to reach and happens in the most miniscule of baby steps. In that manner, it’s a very realistic book; rather than a happily ever after, we end with a subtle ray of hope.<br /><br />I found Love You Hate You Miss You to be a moving and emotional book. I think readers who like books like Speak, Wintergirls, and Cut will find a worthwhile read here. It is high on emotion, not plot though. Readers seeking action or even a more traditional arc of dramatic plot movement will be a little disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9667735887451208639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1210473021" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1210473021" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1210473021?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps " class="user" itemprop="url" name="PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps " href="/user/show/8149327-pinkamy-loves-books-cats-and-naps">PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8149327-pinkamy-loves-books-cats-and-naps?shelf=books-i-can-never-reread-too-many-t">books-i-can-never-reread-too-many-t</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1210473021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5407018605910829913">Grade: B<br/><br/>Amy gets out of rehab 75 days after she killed her best friend Julia. Now instead of being detached, her parents are super interested in everything she does, but Amy isn't buying their faux concern. Her therapist clicks her pen annoyingly and even worse, she recommended Amy for all honors courses instead of the slacker classes she's always taken. Then there are the whispers from the other kids, former friends and some new friends who are trying to befriend her. But, Amy pushes everyone a</span>
  <span id="freeText5407018605910829913" style="display:none">Grade: B<br /><br />Amy gets out of rehab 75 days after she killed her best friend Julia. Now instead of being detached, her parents are super interested in everything she does, but Amy isn't buying their faux concern. Her therapist clicks her pen annoyingly and even worse, she recommended Amy for all honors courses instead of the slacker classes she's always taken. Then there are the whispers from the other kids, former friends and some new friends who are trying to befriend her. But, Amy pushes everyone away. Because she murdered her best friend in a car accident. Even though she wasn't driving.<br /><br />LOVE YOU, HATE YOU, MISS YOU grabbed me from the first page. In journal entries, Amy writes letters to Julia, other chapters are her first person narration. Elizabeth Scott gave Amy a unique, authentic voice, depressed, sarcastic and grieving. Amy was often hard to like but easy to sympathize with, as she shut people out, pushed them away and was downright rude. She had horrible communication skills. Her character is a common archetype in contemporary young adult fiction, and I thought her snail-paced turnaround could have been quicker and more pronounced in stages. The minor characters weren't as fleshed out or unique, nobody transcended stereotypes. <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed Amy's journey and this novel and recommend contemporary YA fans who enjoy books about friends, grief, depression, substance abuse or family.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5407018605910829913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_83549044" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83549044" />
    <a title="Runa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38005-runa"><img alt="Runa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309202154p2/38005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83549044?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Runa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Runa" href="/user/show/38005-runa">Runa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83549044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4930470150375099169">Love You, Hate You, Miss You, catchy title, catchy start, to a catchy plot. Everything about this book screams reality at the reader, honest in tone and easy to read. Even the format, letters to a girl's dead best friend, are heartbreaking. The narration, via the letters, establishes an early level of comfortable interaction. It's a simple, but powerful, tale of a girl struggling to move on with life. For me, the most powerful part of the story was Amy telling her parents of all people, what had</span>
  <span id="freeText4930470150375099169" style="display:none">Love You, Hate You, Miss You, catchy title, catchy start, to a catchy plot. Everything about this book screams reality at the reader, honest in tone and easy to read. Even the format, letters to a girl's dead best friend, are heartbreaking. The narration, via the letters, establishes an early level of comfortable interaction. It's a simple, but powerful, tale of a girl struggling to move on with life. For me, the most powerful part of the story was Amy telling her parents of all people, what had happened with Julia that fateful night. It's breathtaking to watch the growth of the relationship between Amy and her parents springing out of something as tragic as death, as well as the strange post-death evolution of her relationship with Julia. It's a book filled with perceptive thoughts for a very thought-invoking read. Scott really delves into the teens' minds astoundingly well. Some of the dialogue is a little unrealistic, but the overall situations and themes can apply to anyone. Love You, Hate You, Miss You really reminds the audience of the fact that we are all mortals, never knowing when death will strike. It ends with a wham of a final chapter, a final dose of reality, closing on a girl who still has her issues to work out, but knowing that we got to witness the long way she's come.<br /><br />Rating: 5/5 </span>
  <a data-text-id="4930470150375099169" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_297425462" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297425462" />
    <a title="Rayne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5374178-rayne"><img alt="Rayne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440598663p2/5374178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/297425462?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rayne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rayne" href="/user/show/5374178-rayne">Rayne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061122859" href="/book/show/6668136-love-you-hate-you-miss-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=there-s-romance-in-there-somewhere">there-s-romance-in-there-somewhere</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=school-life">school-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=stand-alone-novel">stand-alone-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=you-go-girl">you-go-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=between-3-and-4-stars">between-3-and-4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer297425462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer810899792388730164">I've never been much of a contemporary reader. As a matter of fact, it wasn't until recently that I decided to start giving them a try. As it turns out, I do like them. I prefer my horrors and paranormals and dystopians better, but some contemporaries have managed to sneak into my heart and grab a very nice hold of it *cough*everything by Courtney Summers*cough*. Anyway, the point is that I've stumbled upon some pretty amazing contemporary books this year, and though Love You Hate You Miss You i</span>
  <span id="freeText810899792388730164" style="display:none">I've never been much of a contemporary reader. As a matter of fact, it wasn't until recently that I decided to start giving them a try. As it turns out, I do like them. I prefer my horrors and paranormals and dystopians better, but some contemporaries have managed to sneak into my heart and grab a very nice hold of it *cough*everything by Courtney Summers*cough*. Anyway, the point is that I've stumbled upon some pretty amazing contemporary books this year, and though Love You Hate You Miss You is a really good book, I don't think it achieved the levels of other books about grief like Fall For Anything or Hate List, or captured the pressuring social atmosphere of Some Girls Are, the deep psychological development of Drowning Instinct or Jellicoe Road, or the heart-wrenching power of The Fault in Our Stars. So, though I did like this book, by comparison, it fails to deliver. <br /><br />I liked Amy's voice, but her desperation and guilt and grief never managed to transcend the page for me. The rest of the characters were very one-dimensional and Amy's development was not believable. This is a nice book, and I really liked the ending, especially Caro's choice at the end and Amy's parting words, but I do feel something was missing, something that would've made me truly feel for this book.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="810899792388730164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1240631-holly?shelf=death-ghosts">death-ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1240631-holly?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55283201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4870385910401061607">This was one of the last books I received from the library on my book binge (consisting of roughly 16 books, all to be read within three weeks. Sadly enough, I succeeded). I finally got around to reading <b>Love You Hate You Miss You</b> and I enjoyed.<br/><br/>Amy and her best friend Julia went out partying one night. Only Amy made it home alive. Her parents decide that it's best if she gets some help for her drinking problem. She gets counseling to deal with Julia's death. But nothing helps her overcome the gr</span>
  <span id="freeText4870385910401061607" style="display:none">This was one of the last books I received from the library on my book binge (consisting of roughly 16 books, all to be read within three weeks. Sadly enough, I succeeded). I finally got around to reading <b>Love You Hate You Miss You</b> and I enjoyed.<br /><br />Amy and her best friend Julia went out partying one night. Only Amy made it home alive. Her parents decide that it's best if she gets some help for her drinking problem. She gets counseling to deal with Julia's death. But nothing helps her overcome the grief and guilt she feels. She's got to do that on her own, on her own terms.<br /><br />Amy doesn't come from a broken family. Instead, her parents are so in love with each other they sometimes forget she's around. She was the mistake they made. They love her, but she's lonely.<br /><br />I guess everyone can relate to Amy at some point. She's shunned by people she used to think liked her, becoming a high school outcast. She doesn't have anyone she can confide in anymore, now that Julia's dead. She's breaking, but she's not letting anyone see it. Who can't relate to something like that?<br /><br />Elizabeth Scott wrote a beautiful novel of understanding how everyone makes choices.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4870385910401061607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zdWMB5diwPP2ruU5McOtCH728dnMQhza9kNVUYS/ZPf2F9Yb9jFpOQM4Kf0X5RbWpwxVf7dDZYroiwvC9DDCTA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('M9jP4Cg5nE2BvWrsfu0wX6SRJTC9YZ+tRbMi3hMIDoIIGpX8SWo1h3QrpihYy4uBfWuBlsZg5v1be3xNY4eoOQ==')})
  }

//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_4507'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4507.Sickened?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Sickened: The Memoir of a Munchausen by Proxy Childhood<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/3096.Julie_Gregory?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Julie Gregory<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.73 avg rating &mdash; 16,175 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2003\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer13710049800531853624\">A young girl is perched on the cold chrome of yet another doctor’s examining table, missing yet another day of school. Just twelve, she’s tall, skinny, and weak. It’s four o’clock, and she hasn’t been allowed to eat anything all day. Her mother, on t<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText13710049800531853624\" style=\"display:none\">A young girl is perched on the cold chrome of yet another doctor’s examining table, missing yet another day of school. Just twelve, she’s tall, skinny, and weak. It’s four o’clock, and she hasn’t been allowed to eat anything all day. Her mother, on the other hand, seems curiously excited. She\'s about to suggest open-heart surgery on her child to &quot;get to the bottom of this.&quot; She checks her teeth for lipstick and, as the doctor enters, shoots the girl a warning glance. This child will not ruin her plans.SickenedFrom early childhood, Julie Gregory was continually X-rayed, medicated, and operated on—in the vain pursuit of an illness that was created in her mother’s mind. Munchausen by proxy (MBP) is the world’s most hidden and dangerous form of child abuse, in which the caretaker—almost always the mother—invents or induces symptoms in her child because she craves the attention of medical professionals. Many MBP children die, but Julie Gregory not only survived, she escaped the powerful orbit of her mother\'s madness and rebuilt her identity as a vibrant, healthy young woman.Sickened is a remarkable memoir that speaks in an original and distinctive Midwestern voice, rising to indelible scenes in prose of scathing beauty and fierce humor. Punctuated with Julie\'s actual medical records, it re-creates the bizarre cocoon of her family\'s isolated double-wide trailer, their wild shopping sprees and gun-waving confrontations, the astonishing naïveté of medical professionals and social workers. It also exposes the twisted bonds of terror and love that roped Julie\'s family together—including the love that made a child willing to sacrifice herself to win her mother\'s happiness. The realization that the sickness lay in her mother, not in herself, would not come to Julie until adulthood. But when it did, it would strike like lightning. Through her painful metamorphosis, she discovered the courage to save her own life—and, ultimately, the life of the girl her mother had found to replace her. Sickened takes us to new places in the human heart and spirit. It is an unforgettable story, unforgettably told.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"13710049800531853624\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/363405.Elizabeth_Scott">About Elizabeth Scott</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/363405.Elizabeth_Scott"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1210963737p3/363405.jpg);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/363405.Elizabeth_Scott">Elizabeth Scott

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13533897494491735541">Hey there, I'm Elizabeth. I write young adult novels. I live just outside Washington DC with my husband and dog, and am unable to pass a bookstore without stopping and going inside.<br/><br/>All right, and I can't leave without buying at least one book.<br/><br/>Usually two.
